<p><i><b>Demi</b></i> is the fourth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio album</a> by American singer <a href="/wiki/Demi_Lovato" title="Demi Lovato">Demi Lovato</a>. It was released on May 10, 2013, by <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Records" title="Hollywood Records">Hollywood Records</a>. Looking to transition from her self-described "generic" third album <i><a href="/wiki/Unbroken_(Demi_Lovato_album)" title="Unbroken (Demi Lovato album)">Unbroken</a></i> (2011), Lovato wanted to make her fourth album to "have songs that excited her".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Q.26ABB_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Q.26ABB-2">[2]</a></sup> The album incorporates <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> with elements of <a href="/wiki/Synthpop" title="Synthpop">synthpop</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bubblegum_pop" title="Bubblegum pop">bubblegum pop</a>. The album was recorded between 2012 and 2013, when Lovato served as a judge on the <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S._season_2)" title="The X Factor (U.S. season 2)">second season</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S.)" title="The X Factor (U.S.)">American version</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor" title="The X Factor">The X Factor</a></i>.</p>
<p><i>Demi</i> received generally favorable reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>, who complimented Lovato's vocal performance. The album debuted number three on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with the first-week sales of 110,000 copies—the highest first-week album sales of Lovato's career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The album also reached the top five in Canada, Ireland, Italy, Mexico and Spain. The album's <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Heart_Attack_(Demi_Lovato_song)" title="Heart Attack (Demi Lovato song)">Heart Attack</a>" peaked at number 10 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, marking Lovato's third US top 10 single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Second single "<a href="/wiki/Made_in_the_USA_(song)" title="Made in the USA (song)">Made in the USA</a>" peaked at number 80, while later singles "<a href="/wiki/Neon_Lights_(Demi_Lovato_song)" title="Neon Lights (Demi Lovato song)">Neon Lights</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Really_Don%27t_Care" title="Really Don't Care">Really Don't Care</a>" both reached the top 40 peaking at 36 and 26.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Demi_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In April 2012, Lovato began writing the songs from her fourth studio album, after the commercial success of her third studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Unbroken_(Demi_Lovato_album)" title="Unbroken (Demi Lovato album)">Unbroken</a></i> (2011). The album was recorded during Lovato's appearance as a mentor on the <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S._season_2)" title="The X Factor (U.S. season 2)">second season</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The X Factor (U.S. TV series)">The X Factor</a></i> (U.S.).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Lovato chose the title of the album <i>Demi</i>, because it was her first album intended for a more mainstream audience, and those who did not know her music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Lovato also explained a "sequel" of the song "<a href="/wiki/Skyscraper_(song)" title="Skyscraper (song)">Skyscraper</a>" (2011) is included. After the album was released, it was revealed that "Warrior" was intended to be a sequel of "Skyscraper".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> She stated "I'm incredibly proud of this album" and "It's better than anything I have ever done! I experimented with a variety of different sounds and poured my heart into writing these songs. I'm so excited for everyone to finally get the chance to hear them!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> On May 6, 2013, Lovato asked her <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> followers to "unlock" the entire album by putting song titles in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hashtags" title="Hashtags">hashtags</a>. A special website lovaticsspeeduptime.com was launched, displaying all the songs next to a clock that would turn as tweets would be sent. Once a song became a trending topic, its YouTube video was made available on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VEVO" title="VEVO">VEVO</a>. All the songs were unlocked within four hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/IBooks" title="IBooks">iBooks</a>-exclusive <a href="/wiki/E-book" title="E-book">e-book</a> titled <i>Demi (The Book)</i> was released on June 11, 2013. The book gives fans behind-the-scenes access to the singer, including never-before-seen footage and interviews. In one clip, she says that being honest and open is not only the message she's sending her fans in the book but also on her album. She said, "This album I've had enough time to really reflect on personal experiences and look back at my life after having overcome a bunch of things. I've been more aware of myself; therefore, when you listen to the album, you can really tell in the lyrics and in the emotion and everything I worked really, really hard on this album, and hopefully you'll be able to hear that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Demi_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:24em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I always want to make positive music. Obviously I'm gonna have my songs about heartbreak and break-ups, but with this album... I get sick of listening to the radio and hearing only music that's talking about partying and drinking and getting high. That's not what I do. It's not what I stand for."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;"> —Lovato on the lyricism she wanted to convey with <i>Demi</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Q.26ABB_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Q.26ABB-2">[2]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Lovato herself described <i>Demi</i> as "good old American pop music", which was deeply influenced by her breakout single "<a href="/wiki/Give_Your_Heart_a_Break" title="Give Your Heart a Break">Give Your Heart a Break</a>" and she felt the "super catchy" lyrics as well as the beat of the song resonated with fans, which she wanted to further explore on the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBhab_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBhab-13">[13]</a></sup> According to Lovato, her previous album <i>Unbroken</i> contained songs that she got sick of "a lot faster", so she wanted to "have songs that excited" her on <i>Demi</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TG_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-TG-14">[14]</a></sup> Musical genres on the album range from <a href="/wiki/Pop_rock" title="Pop rock">pop rock</a> to <a href="/wiki/Synthpop" title="Synthpop">synthpop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bubblegum_pop" title="Bubblegum pop">bubblegum pop</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard1_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboard1-1">[1]</a></sup> Apart from "catchy songs" such as the mid-tempo track "Without the Love",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TG_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-TG-14">[14]</a></sup> "emotional songs" are also included on <i>Demi</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBhab_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBhab-13">[13]</a></sup> This is demonstrated on "Shouldn't Come Back" and "Warrior"; which Lovato states are too personal to perform live, comparing them to a song from <i>Unbroken</i> entitled "<a href="/wiki/For_the_Love_of_a_Daughter" title="For the Love of a Daughter">For the Love of a Daughter</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> <i>Billboard</i> states that "Warrior" has Lovato declaring herself "a phoenix that has risen from all-too-public ashes", with emotional lyrics such as: "I've got shame, I've got scars, that I will never show/I'm a survivor, in more ways than you'll know".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard1_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-billboard1-1">[1]</a></sup> Speaking of "Warrior", the singer stated: "That song was probably the hardest and easiest song to write on the album. I was writing about personal experiences, and it's the type of song where you can't fit all of it into one song".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Q.26ABB_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Q.26ABB-2">[2]</a></sup> The theme of Americanism on the album is evident on the track "<a href="/wiki/Made_in_the_USA_(song)" title="Made in the USA (song)">Made in the USA</a>", a <a href="/wiki/Patriotism" title="Patriotism">patriotic</a> love song inspired by "American love stories" in the 1930s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW-16">[16]</a></sup> The song incorporates pop, <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evigan_MTV_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evigan_MTV-17">[17]</a></sup> Stripped down piano ballads on <i>Demi</i> includes, "In Case", which contains lyrics about heartbreak and "<a href="/wiki/Nightingale_(Demi_Lovato_song)" title="Nightingale (Demi Lovato song)">Nightingale</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-music-mixmix_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-music-mixmix-18">[18]</a></sup> The upbeat songs "<a href="/wiki/Really_Don%27t_Care" title="Really Don't Care">Really Don't Care</a>" and "Something That We're Not" are produced to suit of Lovato's "overpowering pipes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard1_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-billboard1-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2013, Lovato stated: "My life has changed so much. I am vulnerable and honest in this record, the way I've always wanted to be. I was ready to come out of the darkness". She referred to the writing process for the album as "therapeutic", further stating: "It helped me get rid of my demons, I am a warrior now. I've been through so much in the past years, it was hard to find the courage to get out of it and write about it, I was afraid no one would understand my message. I spent so much time trying to figure out what the right thing to do was, that I got distracted along the way by fun and temptations and that's why I ended up in rehab at 18".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Demi_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/HitFix" title="HitFix">HitFix</a></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle">B–<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hitfix_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-hitfix-23">[23]</a></sup></td>

</table>
<p>The album received generally positive reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">review aggregator</a> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, the album has a score of 64/100 based on 6 reviews. Jason Lipshutz from <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> gave a positive review, saying that "the singer has a strong grip on her skills as a performer, but is still chiseling away at the formula that works best for her as an artist, and is unwittingly putting that self-discovery on display here."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard1_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-billboard1-1">[1]</a></sup> Jon Caramanica from <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> also gave a positive review, saying that it is "[an] often impressive fourth album."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes1_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-24">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> from <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> gave a more mixed review, rating the album three stars out of five, saying that "Ultimately, this isn't an album of purpose, it's a collection of moments, and it has just enough good ones to solidify Demi Lovato's comeback."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic1_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic1-20">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jody_Rosen" title="Jody Rosen">Jody Rosen</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> awarded the album three stars out of five, saying that "It's predictable stuff—sassy songs, lovelorn songs, a couple of pop-psych pep talks—but Lovato is good company, and her voice has gustiness and character."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone1_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone1-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Melissa Maerz from <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, however, gave the album a mixed review and graded it C+, saying that "it's too bad that her new album <i>Demi</i>, sounds like such a decisive return to teen pop. Transformed from an edgier young woman back into America's sweetheart."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-music-mixmix_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-music-mixmix-18">[18]</a></sup> Marc Hirsh from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> was also mixed, saying that "<i>Demi</i> sounds like Lovato's grasping for hits, when she used to sound like she was making music and having fun."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bostonglobe1_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-bostonglobe1-25">[25]</a></sup> Melinda Newman from <a href="/wiki/HitFix" title="HitFix">HitFix</a> gave the album a B-, commenting "The problem with <i>Demi</i> is that too much of the music here is so generic that it could be any teen queen delivering these tunes." However, she went on to conclude "For those who are looking for a largely uptempo album that fits squarely into much of the pop landscape on radio today, <i>Demi</i> will be a pleasing fit."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Demi_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Neon_Lights_Tour" title="The Neon Lights Tour">The Neon Lights Tour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demi_World_Tour" title="Demi World Tour">Demi World Tour</a></div>
<p>After the album's release in May 2013, Lovato announced she would not go on tour, instead choosing to return as a judge to the third season of The X Factor. In September 2013, Lovato announced <a href="/wiki/The_Neon_Lights_Tour" title="The Neon Lights Tour">The Neon Lights Tour</a> due for a start in February 2014, once The X Factor had finished. It would mark Lovato's first arena tour. The tour included all girl opening acts, with Lovato stating "I want it to be about girl empowerment, I want it to be a huge part."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> These opening acts included girl groups <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Harmony" title="Fifth Harmony">Fifth Harmony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Mix" title="Little Mix">Little Mix</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Cher_Lloyd" title="Cher Lloyd">Cher Lloyd</a> on select dates. The tour covered 41 shows in total across North and South America, as well as Canada and Mexico; beginning in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> on February 9, and closing on May 17 in <a href="/wiki/Monterrey" title="Monterrey">Monterrey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Not long after the closing of the Neon Lights Tour, Lovato announced her first world tour, entitled the <a href="/wiki/Demi_World_Tour" title="Demi World Tour">Demi World Tour</a>. The tour would bring new opening acts, <a href="/wiki/Christina_Perri" title="Christina Perri">Christina Perri</a> and <a href="/wiki/MKTO" title="MKTO">MKTO</a>, as well as playing shows in bigger venues, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Staples_Centre" title="Staples Centre">Staples Centre</a>. It would mark the first time one of Lovato's albums had spawned two separate concert tours. The 2014 dates consisted of 25 shows across North America and Canada, with world tour dates due for 2015. The tour began on September 6 in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, with the first leg concluding on October 27 at the <a href="/wiki/Barclays_Center" title="Barclays Center">Barclays Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> On November 28, 2014, Lovato announced shows in Australia and New Zealand, marking her first time performing in these countries. The leg consists of five shows beginning April 17 in <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, and ending on April 26 in <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> She went on to complete the tour with her most extensive Asian tour to date, performing a total of six shows. The tour concluded on May 19 in <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City" title="Ho Chi Minh City">Ho Chi Minh City</a> to a crowd of 50,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Demi_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The album debuted number three on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with first-week sales of 110,000 copies, behind <a href="/wiki/Vampire_Weekend" title="Vampire Weekend">Vampire Weekend</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Modern_Vampires_of_the_City" title="Modern Vampires of the City">Modern Vampires of the City</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/George_Strait" title="George Strait">George Strait</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Is_Everything_(George_Strait_album)" title="Love Is Everything (George Strait album)">Love Is Everything</a></i>, thus becoming the highest selling opening week of Lovato's career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In the United Kingdom, the album debuted at number ten on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>, with sales of 10,658 copies sold in its first week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Official_Charts_Analysis:_Daft_Punk_LP_sells_165k_to_hit_No.1_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Charts_Analysis:_Daft_Punk_LP_sells_165k_to_hit_No.1-33">[33]</a></sup> With the debut, it became her first album to breach the Top 40 in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Official_Charts_Analysis:_Daft_Punk_LP_sells_165k_to_hit_No.1_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Charts_Analysis:_Daft_Punk_LP_sells_165k_to_hit_No.1-33">[33]</a></sup> The album was certified Gold in the US on September 16, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_sales_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-us_sales-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Demi_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Heart_Attack_(Demi_Lovato_song)" title="Heart Attack (Demi Lovato song)">Heart Attack</a>" was released as the album's lead single on February 24, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The song was written by <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Allan" title="Mitch Allan">Mitch Allan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Evigan" title="Jason Evigan">Jason Evigan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sean_Douglas_(Musician/Songwriter)" title="Sean Douglas (Musician/Songwriter)">Sean Douglas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikki_Williams" title="Nikki Williams">Nikki Williams</a>, Aaron Phillips and Lovato and produced by The Suspex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The song debuted at number 12 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, with first week sales of 215,000 copies, becoming a sales record for Lovato at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The song reached number 10 on the chart, becoming Lovato's third song to do so. The song also reached a peak at number 3 in the United Kingdom, her first single to reach the top ten in the country. The music video was filmed on March 14, 2013<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> and released on April 9, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Lovato performed the song live on several shows, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ellen_DeGeneres_Show" title="The Ellen DeGeneres Show">The Ellen DeGeneres Show</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel_Live!" title="Jimmy Kimmel Live!">Jimmy Kimmel Live!</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The song has since been certified 2× platinum in the United States and Canada, as well as platinum in Denmark, New Zealand and Sweden, gold in Australia, Mexico and Ireland, and silver in the United Kingdom.</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Made_in_the_USA_(song)" title="Made in the USA (song)">Made in the USA</a>" was released as the album's second single on July 16, 2013. Lovato performed the song live at several concerts including <i>Good Morning America'</i>s <i>Summer Concert Series</i> on June 28, 2013, as well as the <a href="/wiki/2013_Teen_Choice_Awards" title="2013 Teen Choice Awards">2013 Teen Choice Awards</a>. The music video was released on July 17, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MadeUSA_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-MadeUSA-43">[43]</a></sup> It peaked at number 80 on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, managed to peak within the top 20 in Belgium, Lebanon and Portugal, as well at number 40 on the US <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40" title="Mainstream Top 40">Mainstream Top 40</a> and number 45 on the US <a href="/wiki/Digital_Songs" title="Digital Songs">Digital Songs</a> charts.</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Neon_Lights_(Demi_Lovato_song)" title="Neon Lights (Demi Lovato song)">Neon Lights</a>" was released as the album's third single on November 19, 2013. On September 29, 2013, Lovato announced the name of her concert tour, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neon_Lights_Tour" title="Neon Lights Tour">Neon Lights Tour</a>, and soon after that "Neon Lights" would become the third single from the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tour_1_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tour_1-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tour_2_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tour_2-46">[46]</a></sup> The song, with its prominent <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">EDM</a> influences, covered new ground for Demi, who had been previously known for her pop ballad singles. The accompanying music video was released on November 21, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NeonLightsVideo_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-NeonLightsVideo-47">[47]</a></sup> In New Zealand, the song peaked at number 12 and was certified gold. It reached number 36 on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, peaking at this position for three non-consecutive weeks. It topped the US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Songs" title="Hot Dance Club Songs">Hot Dance Club Songs</a> and became Lovato's third top 10 single on the <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40" title="Mainstream Top 40">Mainstream Top 40</a>, by reaching at number 7. It was certified platinum in the United States.</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Really_Don%27t_Care" title="Really Don't Care">Really Don't Care</a>" featuring British recording artist <a href="/wiki/Cher_Lloyd" title="Cher Lloyd">Cher Lloyd</a>, was released as the fourth single from the album on May 20, 2014. The week before it was officially serviced to US radio, it charted at number 7 at <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40" title="Mainstream Top 40">Mainstream Top 40</a>, being her fourth top 10 single on the chart. It later on peaked at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> Dance Club Songs. The song debuted on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 at number 98, and has peaked at number 26. Lovato performed the song on several occasions before its official release as a single. Once released in May 2014, performances include on the Season 13 live final of <i>American Idol</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i> Summer Concert Series, <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Night_with_Seth_Meyers" title="Late Night with Seth Meyers">Late Night with Seth Meyers</a></i>, and the <a href="/wiki/2014_Teen_Choice_Awards" title="2014 Teen Choice Awards">2014 Teen Choice Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> "Really Don't Care" was also later certified platinum in the United States.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">Personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Demi_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
